Alice’s Evidence\r","\r","\r","\r","\r","CHAPTER I.\r","Down the Rabbit-Hole\r","\r","\r","Alice was beginning to get very tired of sitting by her sister on the\r","bank, and of having nothing to do: once or twice she had peeped into\r","the book her sister was reading, but it had no pictures or\r","conversations in it, “and what is the use of a book,” thought Alice\r","“without pictures or conversations?”\r","\r","So she was considering in her own mind (as well as she could, for the\r","hot day made her feel very sleepy and stupid), whether the pleasure of\r","making a daisy-chain would be worth the trouble of getting up and\r","picking the daisies, when suddenly a White Rabbit with pink eyes ran\r","close by her.\r","\r","There was nothing so _very_ remarkable in that; nor did Alice think it\r","so _very_ much out of the way to hear the Rabbit say to itself, “Oh\r","dear! Oh dear! I shall be late!” (when she thought it over afterwards,\r","it occurred to her that she ought to have wondered at this, but at the\r","time it all seemed quite natural); but when the Rabbit actually _took a\r","watch out of its waistcoat-pocket_, and looked at it, and then hurried\r","on, Alice started to her feet, for it flashed across her mind that she\r","had never before seen a rabbit with either a waistcoat-pocket, or a\r","watch to take out of it, and burning with curiosity, she ran across the\r","field after it, and fortunately was just in time to see it pop down a\r","large rabbit-hole under the hedge.\r","\r","In another moment down went Alice after it, never once considering how\r","in the world she was to get out again.\r","\r","The rabbit-hole went straight on like a tunnel for some way, and then\r","dipped suddenly down, so suddenly that Alice had not a moment to think\r","about stopping herself before she found herself falling down a very\r","deep well.\r","\r","Either the well was very deep, or she fell very slowly, for she had\r","plenty of time as she went down to look about her and to wonder what\r","was going to happen next. First, she tried to look down and make out\r","what she was coming to, but it was too dark to see anything; then she\r","looked at the sides of the well, and noticed that they were filled with\r","cupboards and book-shelves; here and there she saw maps and pictures\r","hung upon pegs. She took down a jar from one of the shelves as she\r","passed; it was labelled “ORANGE MARMALADE”, but to her great\r","disappointment it was empty: she did not like to drop the jar for fear\r","of killing somebody underneath, so managed to put it into one of the\r","cupboards as she fell past it.\r","\r","“Well!” thought Alice to herself, “after such a fall as this, I shall\r","think nothing of tumbling down stairs! How brave they’ll all think me\r","at home! Why, I wouldn’t say anything about it, even if I fell off the\r","top of the house!” (Which was very likely true.)\r","\r","Down, down, down. Would the fall _never_ come to an end? “I wonder how\r","many miles I’ve fallen by this time?” she said aloud. “I must be\r","getting somewhere near the centre of the earth. Let me see: that would\r","be four thousand miles down, I think—” (for, you see, Alice had learnt\r","several things of this sort in her lessons in the schoolroom, and\r","though this was not a _very_ good opportunity for showing off her\r","knowledge, as there was no one to listen to her, still it was good\r","practice to say it over) “—yes, that’s about the right distance—but\r","then I wonder what Latitude or Longitude I’ve got to?” (Alice had no\r","idea what Latitude was, or Longitude either, but thought they were nice\r","grand words to say.)\r","\r","Presently she began again. “I wonder if I shall fall right _through_\r","the earth! How funny it’ll seem to come out among the people that walk\r","with their heads downward! The Antipathies, I think—” (she was rather\r","glad there _was_ no one listening, this time, as it didn’t sound at all\r","the right word) “—but I shall have to ask them what the name of the\r","country is, you know. Please, Ma’am, is this New Zealand or Australia?”\r","(and she tried to curtsey as she spoke—fancy _curtseying_ as you’re\r","falling through the air! Do you think you could manage it?) “And what\r","an ignorant little girl she’ll think me for asking! No, it’ll never do\r","to ask: perhaps I shall see it written up somewhere.”\r","\r","Down, down, down. There was nothing else to do, so Alice soon began\r","talking again. “Dinah’ll miss me very much to-night, I should think!”\r","(Dinah was the cat.) “I hope they’ll remember her saucer of milk at\r","tea-time. Dinah my dear! I wish you were down here with me! There are\r","no mice in the air, I’m afraid, but you might catch a bat, and that’s\r","very like a mouse, you know. But do cats eat bats, I wonder?” And here\r","Alice began to get rather sleepy, and went on saying to herself, in a\r","dreamy sort of way, “Do cats eat bats? Do cats eat bats?” and\r","sometimes, “Do bats eat cats?” for, you see, as she couldn’t answer\r","either question, it didn’t much matter which way she put it. She felt\r","that she was dozing off, and had just begun to dream that she was\r","walking hand in hand with Dinah, and saying to her very earnestly,\r","“Now, Dinah, tell me the truth: did you ever eat a bat?” when suddenly,\r","thump! thump! down she came upon a heap of sticks and dry leaves, and\r","the fall was over.\r","\r","Alice was not a bit hurt, and she jumped up on to her feet in a moment:\r","she looked up, but it was all dark overhead; before her was another\r","long passage, and the White Rabbit was still in sight, hurrying down\r","it. There was not a moment to be lost: away went Alice like the wind,\r","and was just in time to hear it say, as it turned a corner, “Oh my ears\r","and whiskers, how late it’s getting!” She was close behind it when she\r","turned the corner, but the Rabbit was no longer to be seen: she found\r","herself in a long, low hall, which was lit up by a row of lamps hanging\r","from the roof.\r","\r","There were doors all round the hall, but they were all locked; and when\r","Alice had been all the way down one side and up the other, trying every\r","door, she walked sadly down the middle, wondering how she was ever to\r","get out again.\r","\r","Suddenly she came upon a little three-legged table, all made of solid\r","glass; there was nothing on it except a tiny golden key, and Alice’s\r","first thought was that it might belong to one of the doors of the hall;\r","but, alas! either the locks were too large, or the key was too small,\r","but at any rate it would not open any of them. However, on the second\r","time round, she came upon a low curtain she had not noticed before, and\r","behind it was a little door about fifteen inches high: she tried the\r","little golden key in the lock, and to her great delight it fitted!\r","\r","Alice opened the door and found that it led into a small passage, not\r","much larger than a rat-hole: she knelt down and looked along the\r","passage into the loveliest garden you ever saw. How she longed to get\r","out of that dark hall, and wander about among those beds of bright\r","flowers and those cool fountains, but she could not even get her head\r","through the doorway; “and even if my head would go through,” thought\r","poor Alice, “it would be of very little use without my shoulders. Oh,\r","how I wish I could shut up like a telescope! I think I could, if I only\r","knew how to begin.” For, you see, so many out-of-the-way things had\r","happened lately, that Alice had begun to think that very few things\r","indeed were really impossible.\r","\r","There seemed to be no use in waiting by the little door, so she went\r","back to the table, half hoping she might find another key on it, or at\r","any rate a book of rules for shutting people up like telescopes: this\r","time she found a little bottle on it, (“which certainly was not here\r","before,” said Alice,) and round the neck of the bottle was a paper\r","label, with the words “DRINK ME,” beautifully printed on it in large\r","letters.\r","\r","It was all very well to say “Drink me,” but the wise little Alice was\r","not going to do _that_ in a hurry. “No, I’ll look first,” she said,\r","“and see whether it’s marked ‘_poison_’ or not”; for she had read\r","several nice little histories about children who had got burnt, and\r","eaten up by wild beasts and other unpleasant things, all because they\r","_would_ not remember the simple rules their friends had taught them:\r","such as, that a red-hot poker will burn you if you hold it too long;\r","and that if you cut your finger _very_ deeply with a knife, it usually\r","bleeds; and she had never forgotten that, if you drink much from a\r","bottle marked “poison,” it is almost certain to disagree with you,\r","sooner or later.\r","\r","However, this bottle was _not_ marked “poison,” so Alice ventured to\r","taste it, and finding it very nice, (it had, in fact, a sort of mixed\r","flavour of cherry-tart, custard, pine-apple, roast turkey, toffee, and\r","hot buttered toast,) she very soon finished it off.\r","\r","*      *      *      *      *      *      *\r","\r","    *      *      *      *      *      *\r","\r","*      *      *      *      *      *      *\r","\r","\r","“What a curious feeling!” said Alice; “I must be shutting up like a\r","telescope.”\r","\r","And so it was indeed: she was now only ten inches high, and her face\r","brightened up at the thought that she was now the right size for going\r","through the little door into that lovely garden. First, however, she\r","waited for a few minutes to see if she was going to shrink any further:\r","she felt a little nervous about this; “for it might end, you know,”\r","said Alice to herself, “in my going out altogether, like a candle. I\r","wonder what I should be like then?” And she tried to fancy what the\r","flame of a candle is like after the candle is blown out, for she could\r","not remember ever having seen such a thing.\r","\r","After a while, finding that nothing more happened, she decided on going\r","into the garden at once; but, alas for poor Alice! when she got to the\r","door, she found she had forgotten the little golden key, and when she\r","went back to the table for it, she found she could not possibly reach\r","it: she could see it quite plainly through the glass, and she tried her\r","best to climb up one of the legs of the table, but it was too slippery;\r","and when she had tired herself out with trying, the poor little thing\r","sat down and cried.\r","\r","“Come, there’s no use in crying like that!” said Alice to herself,\r","rather sharply; “I advise you to leave off this minute!” She generally\r","gave herself very good advice, (though she very seldom followed it),\r","and sometimes she scolded herself so severely as to bring tears into\r","her eyes; and once she remembered trying to box her own ears for having\r","cheated herself in a game of croquet she was playing against herself,\r","for this curious child was very fond of pretending to be two people.\r","“But it’s no use now,” thought poor Alice, “to pretend to be two\r","people! Why, there’s hardly enough of me left to make _one_ respectable\r","person!”\r","\r","Soon her eye fell on a little glass box that was lying under the table:\r","she opened it, and found in it a very small cake, on which the words\r","“EAT ME” were beautifully marked in currants. “Well, I’ll eat it,” said\r","Alice, “and if it makes me grow larger, I can reach the key; and if it\r","makes me grow smaller, I can creep under the door; so either way I’ll\r","get into the garden, and I don’t care which happens!”\r","\r","She ate a little bit, and said anxiously to herself, “Which way? Which\r","way?”, holding her hand on the top of her head to feel which way it was\r","growing, and she was quite surprised to find that she remained the same\r","size: to be sure, this generally happens when one eats cake, but Alice\r","had got so much into the way of expecting nothing but out-of-the-way\r","things to happen, that it seemed quite dull and stupid for life to go\r","on in the common way.\r","\r","So she set to work, and very soon finished off the cake.\r","\r","*      *      *      *      *      *      *\r","\r","    *      *      *      *      *      *\r","\r","*      *      *      *      *      *      *\r","\r","\r","\r","\r","CHAPTER II.\r","The Pool of Tears\r","\r","\r","“Curiouser and curiouser!” cried Alice (she was so much surprised, that\r","for the moment she quite forgot how to speak good English); “now I’m\r","opening out like the largest telescope that ever was! Good-bye, feet!”\r","(for when she looked down at her feet, they seemed to be almost out of\r","sight, they were getting so far off). “Oh, my poor little feet, I\r","wonder who will put on your shoes and stockings for you now, dears? I’m\r","sure _I_ shan’t be able! I shall be a great deal too far off to trouble\r","myself about you: you must manage the best way you can;—but I must be\r","kind to them,” thought Alice, “or perhaps they won’t walk the way I\r","want to go! Let me see: I’ll give them a new pair of boots every\r","Christmas.”\r","\r","And she went on planning to herself how she would manage it. “They must\r","go by the carrier,” she thought; “and how funny it’ll seem, sending\r","presents to one’s own feet! And how odd the directions will look!\r","\r","     _Alice’s Right Foot, Esq., Hearthrug, near the Fender,_ (_with\r","     Alice’s love_).\r","\r","Oh dear, what nonsense I’m talking!”\r","\r","Just then her head struck against the roof of the hall: in fact she was\r","now more than nine feet high, and she at once took up the little golden\r","key and hurried off to the garden door.\r","\r","Poor Alice! It was as much as she could do, lying down on one side, to\r","look through into the garden with one eye; but to get through was more\r","hopeless than ever: she sat down and began to cry again.\r","\r","“You ought to be ashamed of yourself,” said Alice, “a great girl like\r","you,” (she might well say this), “to go on crying in this way! Stop\r","this moment, I tell you!” But she went on all the same, shedding\r","gallons of tears, until there was a large pool all round her, about\r","four inches deep and reaching half down the hall.\r","\r","After a time she heard a little pattering of feet in the distance, and\r","she hastily dried her eyes to see what was coming. It was the White\r","Rabbit returning, splendidly dressed, with a pair of white kid gloves\r","in one hand and a large fan in the other: he came trotting along in a\r","great hurry, muttering to himself as he came, “Oh! the Duchess, the\r","Duchess! Oh! won’t she be savage if I’ve kept her waiting!” Alice felt\r","so desperate that she was ready to ask help of any one; so, when the\r","Rabbit came near her, she began, in a low, timid voice, “If you please,\r","sir—” The Rabbit started violently, dropped the white kid gloves and\r","the fan, and skurried away into the darkness as hard as he could go.\r","\r","Alice took up the fan and gloves, and, as the hall was very hot, she\r","kept fanning herself all the time she went on talking: “Dear, dear! How\r","queer everything is to-day! And yesterday things went on just as usual.\r","I wonder if I’ve been changed in the night? Let me think: was I the\r","same when I got up this morning? I almost think I can remember feeling\r","a little different. But if I’m not the same, the next question is, Who\r","in the world am I? Ah, _that’s_ the great puzzle!” And she began\r","thinking over all the children she knew that were of the same age as\r","herself, to see if she could have been changed for any of them.\r","\r","“I’m sure I’m not Ada,” she said, “for her hair goes in such long\r","ringlets, and mine doesn’t go in ringlets at all; and I’m sure I can’t\r","be Mabel, for I know all sorts of things, and she, oh! she knows such a\r","very little! Besides, _she’s_ she, and _I’m_ I, and—oh dear, how\r","puzzling it all is! I’ll try if I know all the things I used to know.\r","Let me see: four times five is twelve, and four times six is thirteen,\r","and four times seven is—oh dear! I shall never get to twenty at that\r","rate! However, the Multiplication Table doesn’t signify: let’s try\r","Geography. London is the capital of Paris, and Paris is the capital of\r","Rome, and Rome—no, _that’s_ all wrong, I’m certain! I must have been\r","changed for Mabel! I’ll try and say ‘_How doth the little_—’” and she\r","crossed her hands on her lap as if she were saying lessons, and began\r","to repeat it, but her voice sounded hoarse and strange, and the words\r","did not come the same as they used to do:—\r","\r","“How doth the little crocodile\r","    Improve his shining tail,\r","And pour the waters of the Nile\r","    On every golden scale!\r","\r","“How cheerfully he seems to grin,\r","    How neatly spread his claws,\r","And welcome little fishes in\r","    With gently smiling jaws!”\r","\r","\r","“I’m sure those are not the right words,” said poor Alice, and her eyes\r","filled with tears again as she went on, “I must be Mabel after all, and\r","I shall have to go and live in that poky little house, and have next to\r","no toys to play with, and oh! ever so many lessons to learn! No, I’ve\r","made up my mind about it; if I’m Mabel, I’ll stay down here! It’ll be\r","no use their putting their heads down and saying ‘Come up again, dear!’\r","I shall only look up and say ‘Who am I then? Tell me that first, and\r","then, if I like being that person, I’ll come up: if not, I’ll stay down\r","here till I’m somebody else’—but, oh dear!” cried Alice, with a sudden\r","burst of tears, “I do wish they _would_ put their heads down! I am so\r","_very_ tired of being all alone here!”\r","\r","As she said this she looked down at her hands, and was surprised to see\r","that she had put on one of the Rabbit’s little white kid gloves while\r","she was talking. “How _can_ I have done that?” she thought. “I must be\r","growing small again.” She got up and went to the table to measure\r","herself by it, and found that, as nearly as she could guess, she was\r","now about two feet high, and was going on shrinking rapidly: she soon\r","found out that the cause of this was the fan she was holding, and she\r","dropped it hastily, just in time to avoid shrinking away altogether.\r","\r","“That _was_ a narrow escape!” said Alice, a good deal frightened at the\r","sudden change, but very glad to find herself still in existence; “and\r","now for the garden!” and she ran with all speed back to the little\r","door: but, alas! the little door was shut again, and the little golden\r","key was lying on the glass table as before, “and things are worse than\r","ever,” thought the poor child, “for I never was so small as this\r","before, never! And I declare it’s too bad, that it is!”\r","\r","As she said these words her foot slipped, and in another moment,\r","splash! she was up to her chin in salt water. Her first idea was that\r","she had somehow fallen into the sea, “and in that case I can go back by\r","railway,” she said to herself. (Alice had been to the seaside once in\r","her life, and had come to the general conclusion, that wherever you go\r","to on the English coast you find a number of bathing machines in the\r","sea, some children digging in the sand with wooden spades, then a row\r","of lodging houses, and behind them a railway station.) However, she\r","soon made out that she was in the pool of tears which she had wept when\r","she was nine feet high.\r","\r","“I wish I hadn’t cried so much!” said Alice, as she swam about, trying\r","to find her way out. “I shall be punished for it now, I suppose, by\r","being drowned in my own tears! That _will_ be a queer thing, to be\r","sure! However, everything is queer to-day.”\r","\r","Just then she heard something splashing about in the pool a little way\r","off, and she swam nearer to make out what it was: at first she thought\r","it must be a walrus or hippopotamus, but then she remembered how small\r","she was now, and she soon made out that it was only a mouse that had\r","slipped in like herself.\r","\r","“Would it be of any use, now,” thought Alice, “to speak to this mouse?\r","Everything is so out-of-the-way down here, that I should think very\r","likely it can talk: at any rate, there’s no harm in trying.” So she\r","began: “O Mouse, do you know the way out of this pool? I am very tired\r","of swimming about here, O Mouse!” (Alice thought this must be the right\r","way of speaking to a mouse: she had never done such a thing before, but\r","she remembered having seen in her brother’s Latin Grammar, “A mouse—of\r","a mouse—to a mouse—a mouse—O mouse!”) The Mouse looked at her rather\r","inquisitively, and seemed to her to wink with one of its little eyes,\r","but it said nothing.\r","\r","“Perhaps it doesn’t understand English,” thought Alice; “I daresay it’s\r","a French mouse, come over with William the Conqueror.” (For, with all\r","her knowledge of history, Alice had no very clear notion how long ago\r","anything had happened.) So she began again: “Où est ma chatte?” which\r","was the first sentence in her French lesson-book. The Mouse gave a\r","sudden leap out of the water, and seemed to quiver all over with\r","fright. “Oh, I beg your pardon!” cried Alice hastily, afraid that she\r","had hurt the poor animal’s feelings. “I quite forgot you didn’t like\r","cats.”\r","\r","“Not like cats!” cried the Mouse, in a shrill, passionate voice. “Would\r","_you_ like cats if you were me?”\r","\r","“Well, perhaps not,” said Alice in a soothing tone: “don’t be angry\r","about it. And yet I wish I could show you our cat Dinah: I think you’d\r","take a fancy to cats if you could only see her. She is such a dear\r","quiet thing,” Alice went on, half to herself, as she swam lazily about\r","in the pool, “and she sits purring so nicely by the fire, licking her\r","paws and washing her face—and she is such a nice soft thing to\r","nurse—and she’s such a capital one for catching mice—oh, I beg your\r","pardon!” cried Alice again, for this time the Mouse was bristling all\r","over, and she felt certain it must be really offended. “We won’t talk\r","about her any more if you’d rather not.”\r","\r","“We indeed!” cried the Mouse, who was trembling down to the end of his\r","tail. “As if _I_ would talk on such a subject! Our family always\r","_hated_ cats: nasty, low, vulgar things! Don’t let me hear the name\r","again!”\r","\r","“I won’t indeed!” said Alice, in a great hurry to change the subject of\r","conversation. “Are you—are you fond—of—of dogs?” The Mouse did not\r","answer, so Alice went on eagerly: “There is such a nice little dog near\r","our house I should like to show you! A little bright-eyed terrier, you\r","know, with oh, such long curly brown hair! And it’ll fetch things when\r","you throw them, and it’ll sit up and beg for its dinner, and all sorts\r","of things—I can’t remember half of them—and it belongs to a farmer, you\r","know, and he says it’s so useful, it’s worth a hundred pounds! He says\r","it kills all the rats and—oh dear!” cried Alice in a sorrowful tone,\r","“I’m afraid I’ve offended it again!” For the Mouse was swimming away\r","from her as hard as it could go, and making quite a commotion in the\r","pool as it went.\r","\r","So she called softly after it, “Mouse dear! Do come back again, and we\r","won’t talk about cats or dogs either, if you don’t like them!” When the\r","Mouse heard this, it turned round and swam slowly back to her: its face\r","was quite pale (with passion, Alice thought), and it said in a low\r","trembling voice, “Let us get to the shore, and then I’ll tell you my\r","history, and you’ll understand why it is I hate cats and dogs.”\r","\r","It was high time to go, for the pool was getting quite crowded with the\r","birds and animals that had fallen into it: there were a Duck and a\r","Dodo, a Lory and an Eaglet, and several other curious creatures. Alice\r","led the way, and the whole party swam to the shore.\r","\r","\r","\r","\r","CHAPTER III.\r","A Caucus-Race and a Long Tale\r","\r","\r","They were indeed a queer-looking party that assembled on the bank—the\r","birds with draggled feathers, the animals with their fur clinging close\r","to them, and all dripping wet, cross, and uncomfortable.\r","\r","The first question of course was, how to get dry again: they had a\r","consultation about this, and after a few minutes it seemed quite\r","natural to Alice to find herself talking familiarly with them, as if\r","she had known them all her life. Indeed, she had quite a long argument\r","with the Lory, who at last turned sulky, and would only say, “I am\r","older than you, and must know better;” and this Alice would not allow\r","without knowing how old it was, and, as the Lory positively refused to\r","tell its age, there was no more to be said.\r","\r","At last the Mouse, who seemed to be a person of authority among them,\r","called out, “Sit down, all of you, and listen to me! _I’ll_ soon make\r","you dry enough!” They all sat down at once, in a large ring, with the\r","Mouse in the middle. Alice kept her eyes anxiously fixed on it, for she\r","felt sure she would catch a bad cold if she did not get dry very soon.\r","\r","“Ahem!” said the Mouse with an important air, “are you all ready? This\r","is the driest thing I know. Silence all round, if you please! ‘William\r","the Conqueror, whose cause was favoured by the pope, was soon submitted\r","to by the English, who wanted leaders, and had been of late much\r","accustomed to usurpation and conquest. Edwin and Morcar, the earls of\r","Mercia and Northumbria—’”\r","\r","“Ugh!” said the Lory, with a shiver.\r","\r","“I beg your pardon!” said the Mouse, frowning, but very politely: “Did\r","you speak?”\r","\r","“Not I!” said the Lory hastily.\r","\r","“I thought you did,” said the Mouse. “—I proceed. ‘Edwin and Morcar,\r","the earls of Mercia and Northumbria, declared for him: and even\r","Stigand, the patriotic archbishop of Canterbury, found it advisable—’”\r","\r","“Found _what_?” said the Duck.\r","\r","“Found _it_,” the Mouse replied rather crossly: “of course you know\r","what ‘it’ means.”\r","\r","“I know what ‘it’ means well enough, when _I_ find a thing,” said the\r","Duck: “it’s generally a frog or a worm. The question is, what did the\r","archbishop find?”\r","\r","The Mouse did not notice this question, but hurriedly went on, “‘—found\r","it advisable to go with Edgar Atheling to meet William and offer him\r","the crown. William’s conduct at first was moderate. But the insolence\r","of his Normans—’ How are you getting on now, my dear?” it continued,\r","turning to Alice as it spoke.\r","\r","“As wet as ever,” said Alice in a melancholy tone: “it doesn’t seem to\r","dry me at all.”\r","\r","“In that case,” said the Dodo solemnly, rising to its feet, “I move\r","that the meeting adjourn, for the immediate adoption of more energetic\r","remedies—”\r","\r","“Speak English!” said the Eaglet. “I don’t know the meaning of half\r","those long words, and, what’s more, I don’t believe you do either!” And\r","the Eaglet bent down its head to hide a smile: some of the other birds\r","tittered audibly.\r","\r","“What I was going to say,” said the Dodo in an offended tone, “was,\r","that the best thing to get us dry would be a Caucus-race.”\r","\r","“What _is_ a Caucus-race?” said Alice; not that she wanted much to\r","know, but the Dodo had paused as if it thought that _somebody_ ought to\r","speak, and no one else seemed inclined to say anything.\r","\r","“Why,” said the Dodo, “the best way to explain it is to do it.” (And,\r","as you might like to try the thing yourself, some winter day, I will\r","tell you how the Dodo managed it.)\r","\r","First it marked out a race-course, in a sort of circle, (“the exact\r","shape doesn’t matter,” it said,) and then all the party were placed\r","along the course, here and there. There was no “One, two, three, and\r","away,” but they began running when they liked, and left off when they\r","liked, so that it was not easy to know when the race was over. However,\r","when they had been running half an hour or so, and were quite dry\r","again, the Dodo suddenly called out “The race is over!” and they all\r","crowded round it, panting, and asking, “But who has won?”\r","\r","This question the Dodo could not answer without a great deal of\r","thought, and it sat for a long time with one finger pressed upon its\r","forehead (the position in which you usually see Shakespeare, in the\r","pictures of him), while the rest waited in silence. At last the Dodo\r","said, “_Everybody_ has won, and all must have prizes.”\r","\r","“But who is to give the prizes?” quite a chorus of voices asked.\r","\r","“Why, _she_, of course,” said the Dodo, pointing to Alice with one\r","finger; and the whole party at once crowded round her, calling out in a\r","confused way, “Prizes! Prizes!”\r","\r","Alice had no idea what to do, and in despair she put her hand in her\r","pocket, and pulled out a box of comfits, (luckily the salt water had\r","not got into it), and handed them round as prizes. There was exactly\r","one a-piece, all round.\r","\r","“But she must have a prize herself, you know,” said the Mouse.\r","\r","“Of course,” the Dodo replied very gravely. “What else have you got in\r","your pocket?” he went on, turning to Alice.\r","\r","“Only a thimble,” said Alice sadly.\r","\r","“Hand it over here,” said the Dodo.\r","\r","Then they all crowded round her once more, while the Dodo solemnly\r","presented the thimble, saying “We beg your acceptance of this elegant\r","thimble;” and, when it had finished this short speech, they all\r","cheered.\r","\r","Alice thought the whole thing very absurd, but they all looked so grave\r","that she did not dare to laugh; and, as she could not think of anything\r","to say, she simply bowed, and took the thimble, looking as solemn as\r","she could.\r","\r","The next thing was to eat the comfits: this caused some noise and\r","confusion, as the large birds complained that they could not taste\r","theirs, and the small ones choked and had to be patted on the back.\r","However, it was over at last, and they sat down again in a ring, and\r","begged the Mouse to tell them something more.\r","\r","“You promised to tell me your history, you know,” said Alice, “and why\r","it is you hate—C and D,” she added in a whisper, half afraid that it\r","would be offended again.\r","\r","“Mine is a long and a sad tale!” said the Mouse, turning to Alice, and\r","sighing.\r","\r","“It _is_ a long tail, certainly,” said Alice, looking down with wonder\r","at the Mouse’s tail; “but why do you call it sad?” And she kept on\r","puzzling about it while the Mouse was speaking, so that her idea of the\r","tale was something like this:—\r","\r","         “Fury said to a mouse, That he met in the house, ‘Let us both\r","         go to law: _I_ will prosecute _you_.—Come, I’ll take no\r","         denial; We must have a trial: For really this morning I’ve\r","         nothing to do.’ Said the mouse to the cur, ‘Such a trial, dear\r","         sir, With no jury or judge, would be wasting our breath.’\r","         ‘I’ll be judge, I’ll be jury,’ Said cunning old Fury: ‘I’ll\r","         try the whole cause, and condemn you to death.’”\r","\r","“You are not attending!” said the Mouse to Alice severely. “What are\r","you thinking of?”\r","\r","“I beg your pardon,” said Alice very humbly: “you had got to the fifth\r","bend, I think?”\r","\r","“I had _not!_” cried the Mouse, sharply and very angrily.\r","\r","“A knot!” said Alice, always ready to make herself useful, and looking\r","anxiously about her. “Oh, do let me help to undo it!”\r","\r","“I shall do nothing of the sort,” said the Mouse, getting up and\r","walking away. “You insult me by talking such nonsense!”\r","\r","“I didn’t mean it!” pleaded poor Alice. “But you’re so easily offended,\r","you know!”\r","\r","The Mouse only growled in reply.\r","\r","“Please come back and finish your story!” Alice called after it; and\r","the others all joined in chorus, “Yes, please do!” but the Mouse only\r","shook its head impatiently, and walked a little quicker.\r","\r","“What a pity it wouldn’t stay!” sighed the Lory, as soon as it was\r","quite out of sight; and an old Crab took the opportunity of saying to\r","her daughter “Ah, my dear! Why,\r","she’ll eat a little bird as soon as look at it!”\r","\r","This speech caused a remarkable sensation among the party. Some of the\r","birds hurried off at once: one old Magpie began wrapping itself up very\r","carefully, remarking, “I really must be getting home; the night-air\r","doesn’t suit my throat!” and a Canary called out in a trembling voice\r","to its children, “Come away, my dears! But I’d better take him\r","his fan and gloves—that is, if I can find them.” As she said this, she\r","came upon a neat little house, on the door of which was a bright brass\r","plate with the name “W. RABBIT,” engraved upon it. She went in without\r","knocking, and hurried upstairs, in great fear lest she should meet the\r","real Mary Ann, and be turned out of the house before she had found the\r","fan and gloves.\r","\r","“How queer it seems,” Alice said to herself, “to be going messages for\r","a rabbit! Come\r","here directly, and get ready for your walk!’ ‘Coming in a minute,\r","nurse! There was no label\r","this time with the words “DRINK ME,” but nevertheless she uncorked it\r","and put it to her lips. “I know _something_ interesting is sure to\r","happen,” she said to herself, “whenever I eat or drink anything; so\r","I’ll just see what this bottle does. She hastily put\r","down the bottle, saying to herself “That’s quite enough—I hope I shan’t\r","grow any more—As it is, I can’t get out at the door—I do wish I hadn’t\r","drunk quite so much!”\r","\r","Alas! it was too late to wish that! She went on growing, and growing,\r","and very soon had to kneel down on the floor: in another minute there\r","was not even room for this, and she tried the effect of lying down with\r","one elbow against the door, and the other arm curled round her head.\r","Still she went on growing, and, as a last resource, she put one arm out\r","of the window, and one foot up the chimney, and said to herself “Now I\r","can do no more, whatever happens. “I can’t remember things as I\r","used—and I don’t keep the same size for ten minutes together!”\r","\r","“Can’t remember _what_ things?” said the Caterpillar.\r","\r","“Well, I’ve tried to say “How doth the little busy bee,” but it all\r","came different!” Alice replied in a very melancholy voice.\r","\r","“Repeat, “_You are old, Father William_,’” said the Caterpillar.\r","\r","Alice folded her hands, and began:—\r","\r","“You are old, Father William,” the young man said,\r","    “And your hair has become very white;\r","And yet you incessantly stand on your head—\r","    Do you think, at your age, it is right?”\r","\r","“In my youth,” Father William replied to his son,\r","    “I feared it might injure the brain;\r","But, now that I’m perfectly sure I have none,\r","    Why, I do it again and again.”\r","\r","“You are old,” said the youth, “as I mentioned before,\r","    And have grown most uncommonly fat;\r","Yet you turned a back-somersault in at the door—\r","    Pray, what is the reason of that?”\r","\r","“In my youth,” said the sage, as he shook his grey locks,\r","    “I kept all my limbs very supple\r","By the use of this ointment—one shilling the box—\r","    Allow me to sell you a couple?”\r","\r","“You are old,” said the youth, “and your jaws are too weak\r","    For anything tougher than suet;\r","Yet you finished the goose, with the bones and the beak—\r","    Pray, how did you manage to do it?”\r","\r","“In my youth,” said his father, “I took to the law,\r","    And argued each case with my wife;\r","And the muscular strength, which it gave to my jaw,\r","    Has lasted the rest of my life.”\r","\r","“You are old,” said the youth, “one would hardly suppose\r","    That your eye was as steady as ever;\r","Yet you balanced an eel on the end of your nose—\r","    What made you so awfully clever?”\r","\r","“I have answered three questions, and that is enough,”\r","    Said his father; Her chin was pressed\r","so closely against her foot, that there was hardly room to open her\r","mouth; but she did it at last, and managed to swallow a morsel of the\r","lefthand bit.\r","\r","*      *      *      *      *      *      *\r","\r","    *      *      *      *      *      *\r","\r","*      *      *      *      *      *      *\r","\r","\r","“Come, my head’s free at last!” said Alice in a tone of delight, which\r","changed into alarm in another moment, when she found that her shoulders\r","were nowhere to be found: all she could see, when she looked down, was\r","an immense length of neck, which seemed to rise like a stalk out of a\r","sea of green leaves that lay far below her.\r","\r","“What _can_ all that green stuff be?” said Alice. “And where _have_ my\r","shoulders got to? There’s no pleasing them!”\r","\r","Alice was more and more puzzled, but she thought there was no use in\r","saying anything more till the Pigeon had finished.\r","\r","“As if it wasn’t trouble enough hatching the eggs,” said the Pigeon;\r","“but I must be on the look-out for serpents night and day! Why, I\r","haven’t had a wink of sleep these three weeks!”\r","\r","“I’m very sorry you’ve been annoyed,” said Alice, who was beginning to\r","see its meaning.\r","\r","“And just as I’d taken the highest tree in the wood,” continued the\r","Pigeon, raising its voice to a shriek, “and just as I was thinking I\r","should be free of them at last, they must needs come wriggling down\r","from the sky! Ugh, Serpent!”\r","\r","“But I’m _not_ a serpent, I tell you!” said Alice. “I’m a—I’m a—”\r","\r","“Well! _What_ are you?” said the Pigeon. “I can see you’re trying to\r","invent something!”\r","\r","“I—I’m a little girl,” said Alice, rather doubtfully, as she remembered\r","the number of changes she had gone through that day.\r","\r","“A likely story indeed!” said the Pigeon in a tone of the deepest\r","contempt. “I’ve seen a good many little girls in my time, but never\r","_one_ with such a neck as that! No, no! You’re a serpent; and there’s\r","no use denying it. I suppose you’ll be telling me next that you never\r","tasted an egg!”\r","\r","“I _have_ tasted eggs, certainly,” said Alice, who was a very truthful\r","child; “but little girls eat eggs quite as much as serpents do, you\r","know.”\r","\r","“I don’t believe it,” said the Pigeon; “but if they do, why then\r","they’re a kind of serpent, that’s all I can say.”\r","\r","This was such a new idea to Alice, that she was quite silent for a\r","minute or two, which gave the Pigeon the opportunity of adding, “You’re\r","looking for eggs, I know _that_ well enough; and what does it matter to\r","me whether you’re a little girl or a serpent?”\r","\r","“It matters a good deal to _me_,” said Alice hastily; “but I’m not\r","looking for eggs, as it happens; and if I was, I shouldn’t want\r","_yours_: I don’t like them raw.”\r","\r","“Well, be off, then!” said the Pigeon in a sulky tone, as it settled\r","down again into its nest. Alice crouched down among the trees as well\r","as she could, for her neck kept getting entangled among the branches,\r","and every now and then she had to stop and untwist it. After a while\r","she remembered that she still held the pieces of mushroom in her hands,\r","and she set to work very carefully, nibbling first at one and then at\r","the other, and growing sometimes taller and sometimes shorter, until\r","she had succeeded in bringing herself down to her usual height.\r","\r","It was so long since she had been anything near the right size, that it\r","felt quite strange at first; but she got used to it in a few minutes,\r","and began talking to herself, as usual. “Come, there’s half my plan\r","done now! How puzzling all these changes are! I’m never sure what I’m\r","going to be, from one minute to another! However, I’ve got back to my\r","right size: the next thing is, to get into that beautiful garden—how\r","_is_ that to be done, I wonder?” As she said this, she came suddenly\r","upon an open place, with a little house in it about four feet high.\r","“Whoever lives there,” thought Alice, “it’ll never do to come upon them\r","_this_ size: why, I should frighten them out of their wits!” So she\r","began nibbling at the righthand bit again, and did not venture to go\r","near the house till she had brought herself down to nine inches high.\r","\r","\r","\r","\r","CHAPTER VI.\r","Pig and Pepper\r","\r","\r","For a minute or two she stood looking at the house, and wondering what\r","to do next, when suddenly a footman in livery came running out of the\r","wood—(she considered him to be a footman because he was in livery:\r","otherwise, judging by his face only, she would have called him a\r","fish)—and rapped loudly at the door with his knuckles. It was opened by\r","another footman in livery, with a round face, and large eyes like a\r","frog; and both footmen, Alice noticed, had powdered hair that curled\r","all over their heads. She felt very curious to know what it was all\r","about, and crept a little way out of the wood to listen.\r","\r","The Fish-Footman began by producing from under his arm a great letter,\r","nearly as large as himself, and this he handed over to the other,\r","saying, in a solemn tone, “For the Duchess. An invitation from the\r","Queen to play croquet.” The Frog-Footman repeated, in the same solemn\r","tone, only changing the order of the words a little, “From the Queen.\r","An invitation for the Duchess to play croquet.”\r","\r","Then they both bowed low, and their curls got entangled together.\r","\r","Alice laughed so much at this, that she had to run back into the wood\r","for fear of their hearing her; and when she next peeped out the\r","Fish-Footman was gone, and the other was sitting on the ground near the\r","door, staring stupidly up into the sky.\r","\r","Alice went timidly up to the door, and knocked.\r","\r","“There’s no sort of use in knocking,” said the Footman, “and that for\r","two reasons. First, because I’m on the same side of the door as you\r","are; secondly, because they’re making such a noise inside, no one could\r","possibly hear you.” And certainly there _was_ a most extraordinary\r","noise going on within—a constant howling and sneezing, and every now\r","and then a great crash, as if a dish or kettle had been broken to\r","pieces.\r","\r","“Please, then,” said Alice, “how am I to get in?”\r","\r","“There might be some sense in your knocking,” the Footman went on\r","without attending to her, “if we had the door between us. For instance,\r","if you were _inside_, you might knock, and I could let you out, you\r","know.” He was looking up into the sky all the time he was speaking, and\r","this Alice thought decidedly uncivil. “But perhaps he can’t help it,”\r","she said to herself; “his eyes are so _very_ nearly at the top of his\r","head. But at any rate he might answer questions.—How am I to get in?”\r","she repeated, aloud.\r","\r","“I shall sit here,” the Footman remarked, “till tomorrow—”\r","\r","At this moment the door of the house opened, and a large plate came\r","skimming out, straight at the Footman’s head: it just grazed his nose,\r","and broke to pieces against one of the trees behind him.\r","\r","“—or next day, maybe,” the Footman continued in the same tone, exactly\r","as if nothing had happened.\r","\r","“How am I to get in?” asked Alice again, in a louder tone.\r","\r","“_Are_ you to get in at all?” said the Footman. “That’s the first\r","question, you know.”\r","\r","It was, no doubt: only Alice did not like to be told so. “It’s really\r","dreadful,” she muttered to herself, “the way all the creatures argue.\r","It’s enough to drive one crazy!”\r","\r","The Footman seemed to think this a good opportunity for repeating his\r","remark, with variations. “I shall sit here,” he said, “on and off, for\r","days and days.”\r","\r","“But what am _I_ to do?” said Alice.\r","\r","“Anything you like,” said the Footman, and began whistling.\r","\r","“Oh, there’s no use in talking to him,” said Alice desperately: “he’s\r","perfectly idiotic!” And she opened the door and went in.\r","\r","The door led right into a large kitchen, which was full of smoke from\r","one end to the other: the Duchess was sitting on a three-legged stool\r","in the middle, nursing a baby; the cook was leaning over the fire,\r","stirring a large cauldron which seemed to be full of soup.\r","\r","“There’s certainly too much pepper in that soup!” Alice said to\r","herself, as well as she could for sneezing.\r","\r","There was certainly too much of it in the air. Even the Duchess sneezed\r","occasionally; and as for the baby, it was sneezing and howling\r","alternately without a moment’s pause. The only things in the kitchen\r","that did not sneeze, were the cook, and a large cat which was sitting\r","on the hearth and grinning from ear to ear.\r","\r","“Please would you tell me,” said Alice, a little timidly, for she was\r","not quite sure whether it was good manners for her to speak first, “why\r","your cat grins like that?”\r","\r","“It’s a Cheshire cat,” said the Duchess, “and that’s why. Pig!”\r","\r","She said the last word with such sudden violence that Alice quite\r","jumped; but she saw in another moment that it was addressed to the\r","baby, and not to her, so she took courage, and went on again:—\r","\r","“I didn’t know that Cheshire cats always grinned; in fact, I didn’t\r","know that cats _could_ grin.”\r","\r","“They all can,” said the Duchess; “and most of ’em do.”\r","\r","“I don’t know of any that do,” Alice said very politely, feeling quite\r","pleased to have got into a conversation.\r","\r","“You don’t know much,” said the Duchess; “and that’s a fact.”\r","\r","Alice did not at all like the tone of this remark, and thought it would\r","be as well to introduce some other subject of conversation. While she\r","was trying to fix on one, the cook took the cauldron of soup off the\r","fire, and at once set to work throwing everything within her reach at\r","the Duchess and the baby—the fire-irons came first; then followed a\r","shower of saucepans, plates, and dishes. The Duchess took no notice of\r","them even when they hit her; and the baby was howling so much already,\r","that it was quite impossible to say whether the blows hurt it or not.\r","\r","“Oh, _please_ mind what you’re doing!” cried Alice, jumping up and down\r","in an agony of terror. “Oh, there goes his _precious_ nose!” as an\r","unusually large saucepan flew close by it, and very nearly carried it\r","off.\r","\r","“If everybody minded their own business,” the Duchess said in a hoarse\r","growl, “the world would go round a deal faster than it does.”\r","\r","“Which would _not_ be an advantage,” said Alice, who felt very glad to\r","get an opportunity of showing off a little of her knowledge. “Just\r","think of what work it would make with the day and night! You see the\r","earth takes twenty-four hours to turn round on its axis—”\r","\r","“Talking of axes,” said the Duchess, “chop off her head!”\r","\r","Alice glanced rather anxiously at the cook, to see if she meant to take\r","the hint; but the cook was busily stirring the soup, and seemed not to\r","be listening, so she went on again: “Twenty-four hours, I _think_; or\r","is it twelve? I—”\r","\r","“Oh, don’t bother _me_,” said the Duchess; “I never could abide\r","figures!” And with that she began nursing her child again, singing a\r","sort of lullaby to it as she did so, and giving it a violent shake at\r","the end of every line:\r","\r","“Speak roughly to your little boy,\r","    And beat him when he sneezes:\r","He only does it to annoy,\r","    Because he knows it teases.”\r","\r","\r","CHORUS.\r","(In which the cook and the baby joined):\r","\r","\r","“Wow! wow! wow!”\r","\r","\r","While the Duchess sang the second verse of the song, she kept tossing\r","the baby violently up and down, and the poor little thing howled so,\r","that Alice could hardly hear the words:—\r","\r","“I speak severely to my boy,\r","    I beat him when he sneezes;\r","For he can thoroughly enjoy\r","    The pepper when he pleases!”\r","\r","\r","CHORUS.\r","\r","\r","“Wow! wow! wow!”\r","\r","\r","“Here! you may nurse it a bit, if you like!” the Duchess said to Alice,\r","flinging the baby at her as she spoke. “I must go and get ready to play\r","croquet with the Queen,” and she hurried out of the room. The cook\r","threw a frying-pan after her as she went out, but it just missed her.\r","\r","Alice caught the baby with some difficulty, as it was a queer-shaped\r","little creature, and held out its arms and legs in all directions,\r","“just like a star-fish,” thought Alice. The poor little thing was\r","snorting like a steam-engine when she caught it, and kept doubling\r","itself up and straightening itself out again, so that altogether, for\r","the first minute or two, it was as much as she could do to hold it.\r","\r","As soon as she had made out the proper way of nursing it, (which was to\r","twist it up into a sort of knot, and then keep tight hold of its right\r","ear and left foot, so as to prevent its undoing itself,) she carried it\r","out into the open air. “If I don’t take this child away with me,”\r","thought Alice, “they’re sure to kill it in a day or two: wouldn’t it be\r","murder to leave it behind?” She said the last words out loud, and the\r","little thing grunted in reply (it had left off sneezing by this time).\r","“Don’t grunt,” said Alice; “that’s not at all a proper way of\r","expressing yourself.”\r","\r","The baby grunted again, and Alice looked very anxiously into its face\r","to see what was the matter with it. There could be no doubt that it had\r","a _very_ turn-up nose, much more like a snout than a real nose; also\r","its eyes were getting extremely small for a baby: altogether Alice did\r","not like the look of the thing at all. “But perhaps it was only\r","sobbing,” she thought, and looked into its eyes again, to see if there\r","were any tears.\r","\r","No, there were no tears. “If you’re going to turn into a pig, my dear,”\r","said Alice, seriously, “I’ll have nothing more to do with you. Mind\r","now!” The poor little thing sobbed again (or grunted, it was impossible\r","to say which), and they went on for some while in silence.\r","\r","Alice was just beginning to think to herself, “Now, what am I to do\r","with this creature when I get it home?” when it grunted again, so\r","violently, that she looked down into its face in some alarm. This time\r","there could be _no_ mistake about it: it was neither more nor less than\r","a pig, and she felt that it would be quite absurd for her to carry it\r","further.\r","\r","So she set the little creature down, and felt quite relieved to see it\r","trot away quietly into the wood. “If it had grown up,” she said to\r","herself, “it would have made a dreadfully ugly child: but it makes\r","rather a handsome pig, I think.” And she began thinking over other\r","children she knew, who might do very well as pigs, and was just saying\r","to herself, “if one only knew the right way to change them—” when she\r","was a little startled by seeing the Cheshire Cat sitting on a bough of\r","a tree a few yards off.\r","\r","The Cat only grinned when it saw Alice. It looked good-natured, she\r","thought: still it had _very_ long claws and a great many teeth, so she\r","felt that it ought to be treated with respect.\r","\r","“Cheshire Puss,” she began, rather timidly, as she did not at all know\r","whether it would like the name: however, it only grinned a little\r","wider. “Come, it’s pleased so far,” thought Alice, and she went on.\r","“Would you tell me, please, which way I ought to go from here?”\r","\r","“That depends a good deal on where you want to get to,” said the Cat.\r","\r","“I don’t much care where—” said Alice.\r","\r","“Then it doesn’t matter which way you go,” said the Cat.\r","\r","“—so long as I get _somewhere_,” Alice added as an explanation.\r","\r","“Oh, you’re sure to do that,” said the Cat, “if you only walk long\r","enough.”\r","\r","Alice felt that this could not be denied, so she tried another\r","question. “What sort of people live about here?”\r","\r","“In _that_ direction,” the Cat said, waving its right paw round, “lives\r","a Hatter: and in _that_ direction,” waving the other paw, “lives a\r","March Hare. Visit either you like: they’re both mad.”\r","\r","“But I don’t want to go among mad people,” Alice remarked.\r","\r","“Oh, you can’t help that,” said the Cat: “we’re all mad here. I’m mad.\r","You’re mad.”\r","\r","“How do you know I’m mad?” said Alice.\r","\r","“You must be,” said the Cat, “or you wouldn’t have come here.”\r","\r","Alice didn’t think that proved it at all; however, she went on “And how\r","do you know that you’re mad?”\r","\r","“To begin with,” said the Cat, “a dog’s not mad. Therefore I’m mad.”\r","\r","“_I_ call it purring, not growling,” said Alice.\r","\r","“Call it what you like,” said the Cat. “Do you play croquet with the\r","Queen to-day?”\r","\r","“I should like it very much,” said Alice, “but I haven’t been invited\r","yet.”\r","\r","“You’ll see me there,” said the Cat, and vanished.\r","\r","Alice was not much surprised at this, she was getting so used to queer\r","things happening. While she was looking at the place where it had been,\r","it suddenly appeared again.\r","\r","“By-the-bye, what became of the baby?” said the Cat. “I’d nearly\r","forgotten to ask.”\r","\r","“It turned into a pig,” Alice quietly said, just as if it had come back\r","in a natural way.\r","\r","“I thought it would,” said the Cat, and vanished again.\r","\r","Alice waited a little, half expecting to see it again, but it did not\r","appear, and after a minute or two she walked on in the direction in\r","which the March Hare was said to live. “I’ve seen hatters before,” she\r","said to herself; “the March Hare will be much the most interesting, and\r","perhaps as this is May it won’t be raving mad—at least not so mad as it\r","was in March.” As she said this, she looked up, and there was the Cat\r","again, sitting on a branch of a tree.\r","\r","“Did you say pig, or fig?” said the Cat.\r","\r","“I said pig,” replied Alice; “and I wish you wouldn’t keep appearing\r","and vanishing so suddenly: you make one quite giddy.”\r","\r","“All right,” said the Cat; and this time it vanished quite slowly,\r","beginning with the end of the tail, and ending with the grin, which\r","remained some time after the rest of it had gone.\r","\r","“Well! It’s the most curious thing I ever saw in my life!”\r","\r","She had not gone much farther before she came in sight of the house of\r","the March Hare: she thought it must be the right house, because the\r","chimneys were shaped like ears and the roof was thatched with fur. Off with his\r","head!’”\r","\r","“How dreadfully savage!” exclaimed Alice.\r","\r","“And ever since that,” the Hatter went on in a mournful tone, “he won’t\r","do a thing I ask! I vote the young lady tells us a story.”\r","\r","“I’m afraid I don’t know one,” said Alice, rather alarmed at the\r","proposal.\r","\r","“Then the Dormouse shall!” they both cried. “Wake up, Dormouse!” And\r","they pinched it on both sides at once.\r","\r","The Dormouse slowly opened his eyes. “I wasn’t asleep,” he said in a\r","hoarse, feeble voice: “I heard every word you fellows were saying.”\r","\r","“Tell us a story!” said the March Hare.\r","\r","“Yes, please do!” pleaded Alice.\r","\r","“And be quick about it,” added the Hatter, “or you’ll be asleep again\r","before it’s done.”\r","\r","“Once upon a time there were three little sisters,” the Dormouse began\r","in a great hurry; “I won’t interrupt again. I\r","dare say there may be _one_.”\r","\r","“One, indeed!” said the Dormouse indignantly. However, he consented to\r","go on. “And so these three little sisters—they were learning to draw,\r","you know—”\r","\r","“What did they draw?” said Alice, quite forgetting her promise.\r","\r","“Treacle,” said the Dormouse, without considering at all this time.\r","\r","“I want a clean cup,” interrupted the Hatter: “let’s all move one place\r","on.”\r","\r","He moved on as he spoke, and the Dormouse followed him: the March Hare\r","moved into the Dormouse’s place, and Alice rather unwillingly took the\r","place of the March Hare. Alice thought this a very curious thing, and she\r","went nearer to watch them, and just as she came up to them she heard\r","one of them say, “Look out now, Five! Two began in a low\r","voice, “Why the fact is, you see, Miss, this here ought to have been a\r","_red_ rose-tree, and we put a white one in by mistake; and if the Queen\r","was to find it out, we should all have our heads cut off, you know. So\r","you see, Miss, we’re doing our best, afore she comes, to—” At this\r","moment Five, who had been anxiously looking across the garden, called\r","out “The Queen! There was a sound of many footsteps,\r","and Alice looked round, eager to see the Queen.\r","\r","First came ten soldiers carrying clubs; these were all shaped like the\r","three gardeners, oblong and flat, with their hands and feet at the\r","corners: next the ten courtiers; these were ornamented all over with\r","diamonds, and walked two and two, as the soldiers did. After these came\r","the royal children; there were ten of them, and the little dears came\r","jumping merrily along hand in hand, in couples: they were all\r","ornamented with hearts. Next came the guests, mostly Kings and Queens,\r","and among them Alice recognised the White Rabbit: it was talking in a\r","hurried nervous manner, smiling at everything that was said, and went\r","by without noticing her. Then followed the Knave of Hearts, carrying\r","the King’s crown on a crimson velvet cushion; and, last of all this\r","grand procession, came THE KING AND QUEEN OF HEARTS.\r","\r","Alice was rather doubtful whether she ought not to lie down on her face\r","like the three gardeners, but she could not remember ever having heard\r","of such a rule at processions; “and besides, what would be the use of a\r","procession,” thought she, “if people had all to lie down upon their\r","faces, so that they couldn’t see it?” So she stood still where she was,\r","and waited.\r","\r","When the procession came opposite to Alice, they all stopped and looked\r","at her, and the Queen said severely “Who is this?” She said it to the\r","Knave of Hearts, who only bowed and smiled in reply.\r","\r","“Idiot!” said the Queen, tossing her head impatiently; and, turning to\r","Alice, she went on, “What’s your name, child?”\r","\r","“My name is Alice, so please your Majesty,” said Alice very politely;\r","but she added, to herself, “Why, they’re only a pack of cards, after\r","all. The Cat seemed to think that there\r","was enough of it now in sight, and no more of it appeared.\r","\r","“I don’t think they play at all fairly,” Alice began, in rather a\r","complaining tone, “and they all quarrel so dreadfully one can’t hear\r","oneself speak—and they don’t seem to have any rules in particular; at\r","least, if there are, nobody attends to them—and you’ve no idea how\r","confusing it is all the things being alive; for instance, there’s the\r","arch I’ve got to go through next walking about at the other end of the\r","ground—and I should have croqueted the Queen’s hedgehog just now, only\r","it ran away when it saw mine coming!”\r","\r","“How do you like the Queen?” said the Cat in a low voice.\r","\r","“Not at all,” said Alice: “she’s so extremely—” Just then she noticed\r","that the Queen was close behind her, listening: so she went on,\r","“—likely to win, that it’s hardly worth while finishing the game.”\r","\r","The Queen smiled and passed on.\r","\r","“Who _are_ you talking to?” said the King, going up to Alice, and\r","looking at the Cat’s head with great curiosity.\r","\r","“It’s a friend of mine—a Cheshire Cat,” said Alice: “allow me to\r","introduce it.”\r","\r","“I don’t like the look of it at all,” said the King: “however, it may\r","kiss my hand if it likes.”\r","\r","“I’d rather not,” the Cat remarked.\r","\r","“Don’t be impertinent,” said the King, “and don’t look at me like\r","that!” He got behind Alice as he spoke.\r","\r","“A cat may look at a king,” said Alice. “I’ve read that in some book,\r","but I don’t remember where.”\r","\r","“Well, it must be removed,” said the King very decidedly, and he called\r","the Queen, who was passing at the moment, “My dear! I wish you would\r","have this cat removed!”\r","\r","The Queen had only one way of settling all difficulties, great or\r","small. “Off with his head!” she said, without even looking round.\r","\r","“I’ll fetch the executioner myself,” said the King eagerly, and he\r","hurried off.\r","\r","Alice thought she might as well go back, and see how the game was going\r","on, as she heard the Queen’s voice in the distance, screaming with\r","passion. Soup\r","does very well without—Maybe it’s always pepper that makes people\r","hot-tempered,” she went on, very much pleased at having found out a new\r","kind of rule, “and vinegar that makes them sour—and camomile that makes\r","them bitter—and—and barley-sugar and such things that make children\r","sweet-tempered. I only wish people knew _that_: then they wouldn’t be\r","so stingy about it, you know—”\r","\r","She had quite forgotten the Duchess by this time, and was a little\r","startled when she heard her voice close to her ear. “You’re thinking\r","about something, my dear, and that makes you forget to talk. I can’t\r","tell you just now what the moral of that is, but I shall remember it in\r","a bit.”\r","\r","“Perhaps it hasn’t one,” Alice ventured to remark.\r","\r","“Tut, tut, child!” said the Duchess. “Everything’s got a moral, if only\r","you can find it.” And she squeezed herself up closer to Alice’s side as\r","she spoke.\r","\r","Alice did not much like keeping so close to her: first, because the\r","Duchess was _very_ ugly; and secondly, because she was exactly the\r","right height to rest her chin upon Alice’s shoulder, and it was an\r","uncomfortably sharp chin. However, she did not like to be rude, so she\r","bore it as well as she could.\r","\r","“The game’s going on rather better now,” she said, by way of keeping up\r","the conversation a little.\r","\r","“’Tis so,” said the Duchess: “and the moral of that is—‘Oh, ’tis love,\r","’tis love, that makes the world go round!’”\r","\r","“Somebody said,” Alice whispered, “that it’s done by everybody minding\r","their own business!”\r","\r","“Ah, well! It means much the same thing,” said the Duchess, digging her\r","sharp little chin into Alice’s shoulder as she added, “and the moral of\r","_that_ is—‘Take care of the sense, and the sounds will take care of\r","themselves.’”\r","\r","“How fond she is of finding morals in things!” Alice thought to\r","herself.\r","\r","“I dare say you’re wondering why I don’t put my arm round your waist,”\r","the Duchess said after a pause: “the reason is, that I’m doubtful about\r","the temper of your flamingo. And\r","the moral of that is—‘Birds of a feather flock together.’”\r","\r","“Only mustard isn’t a bird,” Alice remarked.\r","\r","“Right, as usual,” said the Duchess: “what a clear way you have of\r","putting things!”\r","\r","“It’s a mineral, I _think_,” said Alice.\r","\r","“Of course it is,” said the Duchess, who seemed ready to agree to\r","everything that Alice said; “there’s a large mustard-mine near here.\r","And the moral of that is—‘The more there is of mine, the less there is\r","of yours.’”\r","\r","“Oh, I know!” exclaimed Alice, who had not attended to this last\r","remark, “it’s a vegetable. It doesn’t look like one, but it is.”\r","\r","“I quite agree with you,” said the Duchess; “and the moral of that\r","is—‘Be what you would seem to be’—or if you’d like it put more\r","simply—‘Never imagine yourself not to be otherwise than what it might\r","appear to others that what you were or might have been was not\r","otherwise than what you had been would have appeared to them to be\r","otherwise.’”\r","\r","“I think I should understand that better,” Alice said very politely,\r","“if I had it written down: but I can’t quite follow it as you say it.”\r","\r","“That’s nothing to what I could say if I chose,” the Duchess replied,\r","in a pleased tone.\r","\r","“Pray don’t trouble yourself to say it any longer than that,” said\r","Alice.\r","\r","“Oh, don’t talk about trouble!” said the Duchess. “I make you a present\r","of everything I’ve said as yet.”\r","\r","“A cheap sort of present!” thought Alice. “I’m glad they don’t give\r","birthday presents like that!” But she did not venture to say it out\r","loud.\r","\r","“Thinking again?” the Duchess asked, with another dig of her sharp\r","little chin.\r","\r","“I’ve a right to think,” said Alice sharply, for she was beginning to\r","feel a little worried.\r","\r","“Just about as much right,” said the Duchess, “as pigs have to fly; and\r","the m—”\r","\r","But here, to Alice’s great surprise, the Duchess’s voice died away,\r","even in the middle of her favourite word ‘moral,’ and the arm that was\r","linked into hers began to tremble. Alice looked up, and there stood the\r","Queen in front of them, with her arms folded, frowning like a\r","thunderstorm.\r","\r","“A fine day, your Majesty!” the Duchess began in a low, weak voice.\r","\r","“Now, I give you fair warning,” shouted the Queen, stamping on the\r","ground as she spoke; “either you or your head must be off, and that in\r","about half no time! Take your choice!”\r","\r","The Duchess took her choice, and was gone in a moment.\r","\r","“Let’s go on with the game,” the Queen said to Alice; and Alice was too\r","much frightened to say a word, but slowly followed her back to the\r","croquet-ground.\r","\r","The other guests had taken advantage of the Queen’s absence, and were\r","resting in the shade: however, the moment they saw her, they hurried\r","back to the game, the Queen merely remarking that a moment’s delay\r","would cost them their lives.\r","\r","All the time they were playing the Queen never left off quarrelling\r","with the other players, and shouting “Off with his head!” or “Off with\r","her head!” Those whom she sentenced were taken into custody by the\r","soldiers, who of course had to leave off being arches to do this, so\r","that by the end of half an hour or so there were no arches left, and\r","all the players, except the King, the Queen, and Alice, were in custody\r","and under sentence of execution.\r","\r","Then the Queen left off, quite out of breath, and said to Alice, “Have\r","you seen the Mock Turtle yet?”\r","\r","“No,” said Alice. “I don’t even know what a Mock Turtle is.”\r","\r","“It’s the thing Mock Turtle Soup is made from,” said the Queen.\r","\r","“I never saw one, or heard of one,” said Alice.\r","\r","“Come on, then,” said the Queen, “and he shall tell you his history,”\r","\r","As they walked off together, Alice heard the King say in a low voice,\r","to the company generally, “You are all pardoned.” “Come, _that’s_ a\r","good thing!” she said to herself, for she had felt quite unhappy at the\r","number of executions the Queen had ordered.\r","\r","They very soon came upon a Gryphon, lying fast asleep in the sun. (If\r","you don’t know what a Gryphon is, look at the picture.) “Up, lazy\r","thing!” said the Queen, “and take this young lady to see the Mock\r","Turtle, and to hear his history. I must go back and see after some\r","executions I have ordered;” and she walked off, leaving Alice alone\r","with the Gryphon. Alice did not quite like the look of the creature,\r","but on the whole she thought it would be quite as safe to stay with it\r","as to go after that savage Queen: so she waited.\r","\r","The Gryphon sat up and rubbed its eyes: then it watched the Queen till\r","she was out of sight: then it chuckled. “What fun!” said the Gryphon,\r","half to itself, half to Alice.\r","\r","“What _is_ the fun?” said Alice.\r","\r","“Why, _she_,” said the Gryphon. “It’s all her fancy, that: they never\r","executes nobody, you know. Come on!”\r","\r","“Everybody says ‘come on!’ here,” thought Alice, as she went slowly\r","after it: “I never was so ordered about in all my life, never!”\r","\r","They had not gone far before they saw the Mock Turtle in the distance,\r","sitting sad and lonely on a little ledge of rock, and, as they came\r","nearer, Alice could hear him sighing as if his heart would break. She\r","pitied him deeply. “What is his sorrow?” she asked the Gryphon, and the\r","Gryphon answered, very nearly in the same words as before, “It’s all\r","his fancy, that: he hasn’t got no sorrow, you know. Come on!”\r","\r","So they went up to the Mock Turtle, who looked at them with large eyes\r","full of tears, but said nothing.\r","\r","“This here young lady,” said the Gryphon, “she wants for to know your\r","history, she do.”\r","\r","“I’ll tell it her,” said the Mock Turtle in a deep, hollow tone: “sit\r","down, both of you, and don’t speak a word till I’ve finished.”\r","\r","So they sat down, and nobody spoke for some minutes. Alice thought to\r","herself, “I don’t see how he can _ever_ finish, if he doesn’t begin.”\r","But she waited patiently.\r","\r","“Once,” said the Mock Turtle at last, with a deep sigh, “I was a real\r","Turtle.”\r","\r","These words were followed by a very long silence, broken only by an\r","occasional exclamation of “Hjckrrh!” from the Gryphon, and the constant\r","heavy sobbing of the Mock Turtle. Alice was very nearly getting up and\r","saying, “Thank you, sir, for your interesting story,” but she could not\r","help thinking there _must_ be more to come, so she sat still and said\r","nothing.\r","\r","“When we were little,” the Mock Turtle went on at last, more calmly,\r","though still sobbing a little now and then, “we went to school in the\r","sea. The master was an old Turtle—we used to call him Tortoise—”\r","\r","“Why did you call him Tortoise, if he wasn’t one?” Alice asked.\r","\r","“We called him Tortoise because he taught us,” said the Mock Turtle\r","angrily: “really you are very dull!”\r","\r","“You ought to be ashamed of yourself for asking such a simple\r","question,” added the Gryphon; and then they both sat silent and looked\r","at poor Alice, who felt ready to sink into the earth. At last the\r","Gryphon said to the Mock Turtle, “Drive on, old fellow! Don’t be all\r","day about it!” and he went on in these words:\r","\r","“Yes, we went to school in the sea, though you mayn’t believe it—”\r","\r","“I never said I didn’t!” interrupted Alice.\r","\r","“You did,” said the Mock Turtle.\r","\r","“Hold your tongue!” added the Gryphon, before Alice could speak again.\r","The Mock Turtle went on.\r","\r","“We had the best of educations—in fact, we went to school every day—”\r","\r","“_I’ve_ been to a day-school, too,” said Alice; “you needn’t be so\r","proud as all that.”\r","\r","“With extras?” asked the Mock Turtle a little anxiously.\r","\r","“Yes,” said Alice, “we learned French and music.”\r","\r","“And washing?” said the Mock Turtle.\r","\r","“Certainly not!” said Alice indignantly.\r","\r","“Ah! then yours wasn’t a really good school,” said the Mock Turtle in a\r","tone of great relief. “Now at _ours_ they had at the end of the bill,\r","‘French, music, _and washing_—extra.’”\r","\r","“You couldn’t have wanted it much,” said Alice; “living at the bottom\r","of the sea.”\r","\r","“I couldn’t afford to learn it.” said the Mock Turtle with a sigh. “I\r","only took the regular course.”\r","\r","“What was that?” inquired Alice.\r","\r","“Reeling and Writhing, of course, to begin with,” the Mock Turtle\r","replied; “and then the different branches of Arithmetic—Ambition,\r","Distraction, Uglification, and Derision.”\r","\r","“I never heard of ‘Uglification,’” Alice ventured to say. “What is it?”\r","\r","The Gryphon lifted up both its paws in surprise. “What! Never heard of\r","uglifying!” it exclaimed. “You know what to beautify is, I suppose?”\r","\r","“Yes,” said Alice doubtfully: “it means—to—make—anything—prettier.”\r","\r","“Well, then,” the Gryphon went on, “if you don’t know what to uglify\r","is, you _are_ a simpleton.”\r","\r","Alice did not feel encouraged to ask any more questions about it, so\r","she turned to the Mock Turtle, and said “What else had you to learn?”\r","\r","“Well, there was Mystery,” the Mock Turtle replied, counting off the\r","subjects on his flappers, “—Mystery, ancient and modern, with\r","Seaography: then Drawling—the Drawling-master was an old conger-eel,\r","that used to come once a week: _he_ taught us Drawling, Stretching, and\r","Fainting in Coils.”\r","\r","“What was _that_ like?” said Alice.\r","\r","“Well, I can’t show it you myself,” the Mock Turtle said: “I’m too\r","stiff. And the Gryphon never learnt it.”\r","\r","“Hadn’t time,” said the Gryphon: “I went to the Classics master,\r","though. He was an old crab, _he_ was.”\r","\r","“I never went to him,” the Mock Turtle said with a sigh: “he taught\r","Laughing and Grief, they used to say.”\r","\r","“So he did, so he did,” said the Gryphon, sighing in his turn; and both\r","creatures hid their faces in their paws.\r","\r","“And how many hours a day did you do lessons?” said Alice, in a hurry\r","to change the subject.\r","\r","“Ten hours the first day,” said the Mock Turtle: “nine the next, and so\r","on.”\r","\r","“What a curious plan!” exclaimed Alice.\r","\r","“That’s the reason they’re called lessons,” the Gryphon remarked:\r","“because they lessen from day to day.”\r","\r","This was quite a new idea to Alice, and she thought it over a little\r","before she made her next remark. “Then the eleventh day must have been\r","a holiday?”\r","\r","“Of course it was,” said the Mock Turtle.\r","\r","“And how did you manage on the twelfth?” Alice went on eagerly.\r","\r","“That’s enough about lessons,” the Gryphon interrupted in a very\r","decided tone: “tell her something about the games now.”\r","\r","\r","\r","\r","CHAPTER X.\r","The Lobster Quadrille\r","\r","\r","The Mock Turtle sighed deeply, and drew the back of one flapper across\r","his eyes. He looked at Alice, and tried to speak, but for a minute or\r","two sobs choked his voice. “Same as if he had a bone in his throat,”\r","said the Gryphon: and it set to work shaking him and punching him in\r","the back. At last the Mock Turtle recovered his voice, and, with tears\r","running down his cheeks, he went on again:—\r","\r","“You may not have lived much under the sea—” (“I haven’t,” said\r","Alice)—“and perhaps you were never even introduced to a lobster—”\r","(Alice began to say “I once tasted—” but checked herself hastily, and\r","said “No, never”) “—so you can have no idea what a delightful thing a\r","Lobster Quadrille is!”\r","\r","“No, indeed,” said Alice. “What sort of a dance is it?”\r","\r","“Why,” said the Gryphon, “you first form into a line along the\r","sea-shore—”\r","\r","“Two lines!” cried the Mock Turtle. “Seals, turtles, salmon, and so on;\r","then, when you’ve cleared all the jelly-fish out of the way—”\r","\r","“_That_ generally takes some time,” interrupted the Gryphon.\r","\r","“—you advance twice—”\r","\r","“Each with a lobster as a partner!” cried the Gryphon.\r","\r","“Of course,” the Mock Turtle said: “advance twice, set to partners—”\r","\r","“—change lobsters, and retire in same order,” continued the Gryphon.\r","\r","“Then, you know,” the Mock Turtle went on, “you throw the—”\r","\r","“The lobsters!” shouted the Gryphon, with a bound into the air.\r","\r","“—as far out to sea as you can—”\r","\r","“Swim after them!” screamed the Gryphon.\r","\r","“Turn a somersault in the sea!” cried the Mock Turtle, capering wildly\r","about.\r","\r","“Change lobsters again!” yelled the Gryphon at the top of its voice.\r","\r","“Back to land again, and that’s all the first figure,” said the Mock\r","Turtle, suddenly dropping his voice;
